## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator. The acceleration dv_dt depends on position x (restoring force), velocity v (damping), and possibly time t (external driving), with nonlinearities in the restoring force and/or damping terms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Driven harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (with periodic driving)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic stiffness + damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing equation)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Quadratic-cubic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric potential)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (Rayleigh-type dissipation)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x (time-modulated stiffness)
- Coupled nonlinear terms: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 * v + c2 * v (position-dependent damping)
- Helmholtz oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * v (quadratic nonlinearity with damping)
- General driven nonlinear: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * (1 - c3 * x**2) * v + c4 * cos(c5 * t) (combined Duffing-Van der Pol with driving)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Symmetric restoring potential → only odd powers of x appear (x, x³, x⁵) in the acceleration expression
- Asymmetric restoring potential → even powers of x (x²) also appear alongside odd powers
- Self-sustained oscillations (limit cycles) → velocity-dependent terms with sign changes, e.g., (1 - c*x²)*v structure
- External periodic driving → additive sinusoidal or cosinusoidal functions of time: sin(c*t), cos(c*t)
- Parametric excitation → time-dependent coefficient multiplying position: cos(c*t)*x
- Hardening spring behavior → positive coefficient on x³ with negative coefficient on x (Duffing-type)
- Softening spring behavior → negative coefficient on x³ indicating potential well flattening
- Nonlinear damping with amplitude dependence → terms like x²*v indicating damping that varies with displacement
- Energy-dependent frequency shift → presence of x³ or higher odd powers modifying the effective spring constant
- Phase-space symmetry breaking → mixed terms like x*v or x*v² indicating non-conservative coupling
